League of Nations Administrative Council Resolves to Increase China's Council Seat, with a Term of Three Years, Final Decision by the General Assembly in September 6

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council held an open meeting today to discuss the issue of China's request for a seat on the Administrative Council. It was approved and resolved to submit it to the League of Nations General Assembly for review in September, and then make a final decision. After the meeting today, Foreign Minister Eden, as chairman, first presented the report of the Administrative Council Committee (i.e., the one that reviews the allocation of Council seats) and read it aloud. This report should have been read by the chairman of the committee, i.e., the Italian representative. However, the entire delegation of that country had returned home, so Foreign Minister Eden read it on his behalf. The report stated that the committee agreed to temporarily add two non-permanent Council seats, from September 1936 to September 1939. One would be given to a European country that does not belong to any group. This seat was added in 1933 and is currently held by Portugal. It should continue to be maintained for the next three years. The other seat should be given to a country on the Asian continent. In the committee's view, it could be given to China. The above method should be decided by the Administrative Council after review by the League of Nations General Assembly. After Eden finished reading the report, Portuguese representative Vasconcelos stood up and spoke, saying that the method proposed by the committee was unfair. Among the member states of the League of Nations, Asian countries account for only five, while European countries that do not belong to any group total fourteen. According to the method proposed by the committee, Asian countries will occupy two non-permanent Council seats, while European countries that do not belong to any group will only occupy one seat. How can this be called fair? However, he did not oppose China obtaining a non-permanent Council seat. Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü argued that the term of the newly added non-permanent Council seat should be set at three years. Roma is a foreign minister,　　　　　　　　Cheng took the Council seat　to give to China, and said that for European countries that do not belong to any group, the term of their Council seat should be less than three years. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov also expressed his support for China's request and argued that the term of European non-permanent Council seats should be limited to one year. Eden then said that the Administrative Council should not make any decision on the issue of the term of the Council seat. The report submitted by the committee and the opinions of the representatives of various countries should be submitted to the League of Nations General Assembly for processing. The Administrative Council decided to do so, and then adjourned the meeting. (Havas dispatch of the 13th)

Baldwin Announces League of Nations Reform Plan, to be Decided by the General Assembly in September, Military Sanctions Are Necessary 7

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin said in a speech at Albert Hall today that when the League of Nations General Assembly meets in the autumn, it must consider whether the League of Nations needs to be changed and how to change it. He hoped that such changes would enable non-member states to join as well. Military sanctions are a necessary part of collective security and are ultimately unavoidable. The work thereafter is to re-examine the entire issue of sanctions and collective security based on past experience. The results that may be obtained in the future will be of great importance to the future situation in Europe. (Reuters dispatch of the 14th)

(London) The Conservative Women's Association recently held a meeting at Albert Hall. Prime Minister Baldwin attended and delivered a speech, stating that since the League of Nations has achieved nothing in handling the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, the League of Nations General Assembly must make necessary revisions to the covenant when it holds its regular meeting in September of this year. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

(Geneva) Danish representative Munch and Spanish representative Madariaga recently invited Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov to lunch and discussed the League of Nations reform plan drafted by the representatives of Denmark, Norway, Sweden, Finland, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and Spain. According to the representatives of these countries, they had previously jointly decided that Articles 11 and 19 of the League of Nations Covenant should be strengthened to prevent international disputes. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

League of Nations Administrative Council Ends Current Session, Eden Busy Meeting with Representatives of Various Countries 8

(Geneva) After the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting today hotly debated the report submitted by the Italian government to the Slave Commission, it adjourned to June 15, when it will continue to discuss the Italian-Ethiopian case. The result of the debate on the Italian report was to send the document to the members of the Slave Commission with a note stating, "This document was sent by the military authorities who violated the League of Nations Covenant and occupied foreign territory." Some delegations in the League of Nations will leave here tonight. However, British Foreign Minister Eden, after a busy day, still has to fulfill some appointments, so he will stay here until tomorrow before starting his journey. Eden spent the entire morning today meeting with guests, including Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, Greek representative Politis, League of Nations Commissioner in Danzig Lester, and Danzig Senate President Greiser. (Reuters dispatch of the 13th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council held a non-public meeting at 5:00 p.m. today and decided to hold an extraordinary meeting on June 16 to discuss the entire Italian-Ethiopian issue and the Locarno case as a whole. During the meeting, British Foreign Minister Eden, as chairman, presented the report drafted by the Advisory Committee on the Issue of Slave Trade and said that the report listed several documents on the slave trade situation in Abyssinia, which were submitted by Italy at a time when Italy was violating the Covenant and engaged in war against Ethiopia. Therefore, the report should be announced, and he requested the Administrative Council to decide. It was decided that the report would still be published, but with a statement that the Administrative Council's view on the Italian-Ethiopian dispute would not be changed by the documents submitted by Italy. The Administrative Council then decided to extend the mission of Lester, the High Commissioner of the League of Nations in the Free City of Danzig, by one year and to convene an international conference with Norwegian Reistad as chairman to discuss an international convention using radio broadcasting as a tool to promote peace. Thereupon, the Administrative Council held an open meeting, passed various reports, and the current session was concluded. (Havas dispatch of the 13th)

(Geneva) The 90th regular session of the League of Nations Administrative Council has concluded. French Minister without Portfolio Peng Gu left for Paris by plane at 10:00 a.m. today. Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck also returned home this morning. British Foreign Minister Eden is scheduled to return to England this evening and will meet with League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol, Spanish representative Madariaga, and representatives of several countries before his departure. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

Italian People Demand the Cancellation of Sanctions, the Chamber of Deputies Approves the Annexation of Ethiopia, the Relationship with the League of Nations Remains Ambiguous 9

(Rome) The Italian people are now demanding that all countries cancel sanctions and recognize the annexation of Ethiopia. Whether Italy will continue to be a member of the League of Nations remains uncertain. It is expected that after the Italian Chamber of Deputies passes the order to annex Ethiopia today, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will make an important statement on this issue. This order, as an urgent plan, will be passed by the Chamber of Deputies in a continuous reading. According to sources from responsible circles, the League of Nations Administrative Council's maintenance of sanctions is forcing Italy to suspend cooperation with the League of Nations. However, various speculations about the departure of the Italian delegation from Geneva are still premature. The semi-official Italian newspaper Il Giornale d'Italia today published an article by Gaeta, stating that the Italian government is now seriously considering the issue of withdrawing from the League of Nations. (Reuters dispatch of the 14th)

(Rome) Prime Minister Mussolini will announce in the Chamber of Deputies tomorrow whether Italy will remain a member of the League of Nations. Official sources here stated that only he knows Mussolini's plans. Although he is deeply indignant at the League of Nations' decision to maintain sanctions, diplomatic circles doubt whether Italy will withdraw from the League of Nations, but they also acknowledge that the situation is very serious. The editor of Mussolini's mouthpiece, Il Giornale d'Italia, Gaeta, published an article today, saying that Italy is tired of the League of Nations. The Italian people have calmly accepted the League of Nations' unfair judgment on Italy. The departure of the Italian delegation from Geneva can be regarded as the prelude to Italy's withdrawal from the League of Nations. Italian Chief Representative Aloisi declined to comment on his departure from Geneva, saying only that he was ordered to return home and knew nothing else. As to whether he would still go to Geneva, Aloisi declined to answer, but another representative said, "I doubt it very much. The situation is indeed very serious." (National Electric dispatch of the 13th)

(Rome) Regarding the withdrawal of the Italian delegation to the League of Nations, semi-official sources recently stated that it is impossible to determine what this move means at this time. Since the League of Nations' views on the Ethiopian issue are still contradictory to Italy's views, Italy has no choice but to suspend cooperation with the League of Nations. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

(Rome) After Prime Minister Mussolini announced the annexation of Ethiopia on the 9th of this month and appointed General Badoglio as the Governor of Ethiopia, the Chamber of Deputies is scheduled to hold a grand meeting this afternoon to approve it. All members of parliament and spectators will be required to wear fascist party uniforms. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

The Italian military authorities in Addis Ababa recently decided that foreign merchants who sell military equipment to Ethiopian soldiers or are known for being anti-Italian will be deported. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

Jerusalem. When the Ethiopian Emperor arrived here a few days ago, British High Commissioner for Palestine Sir Arthur Wauchope officially received him. The Italian Consul General recently protested this matter. (Havas dispatch of the 14th)

British Statement on the Italian Annexation of Ethiopia, Baldwin Says British Policy is Based on the League of Nations 10

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin said in the House of Commons yesterday in response to various questions about the Italian-Ethiopian incident that when the Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, delivered the Italian order to declare the annexation of Ethiopia and the appointment of the Italian King with the title of Emperor of Ethiopia to the Foreign Office on Tuesday, the Foreign Office told him that Britain received the document with various reservations and would submit it to Foreign Minister Eden for his consideration and handling after he returned to London from Geneva. The Prime Minister then mentioned the content of the letter from General Badoglio, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, received by the British Embassy and other embassies in Addis Ababa, saying that the British government had instructed the British Minister to Ethiopia, Barton, to make it clear that he recognized General Badoglio as the authority in military occupation of Addis Ababa and that his current dealings with General Badoglio were based on this position. The Prime Minister also answered another question from the opposition party, saying that the British government had repeatedly stated that Britain's policy on the Italian-Ethiopian dispute was based on the collective decisions of the League of Nations. (Reuters dispatch of the 14th)

(London) According to reliable sources, the government will soon send a memorandum to the Italian government regarding the Italian annexation of Ethiopia. When the Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, delivered a copy of the annexation order to the Foreign Office the other day, Sir Oliphant, the legal advisor to the Foreign Office, stated his reservations. The cabinet meeting today has already ratified Oliphant's move. As soon as Foreign Minister Eden returns to the country from Geneva, the Italian Ambassador will be notified that the incoming letter has been read, but the reservation will be raised again, and the memorandum will be submitted in a few days. As far as the general opinions of the Foreign Office on the Italian-Ethiopian issue are concerned, they are now advocating a friendly solution with Italy. These people have said that the door to negotiations between Britain and Italy is not willing to be closed at this time, and everything that can cause a split should be avoided. Political leaders also said that there is now a movement in the country that advocates that the views on the current situation should be closer to reality. This movement will inevitably expand in the coming weeks. As a result, when the League of Nations Administrative Council meets on June 16, Foreign Minister Eden's attitude may be influenced by it. (Havas dispatch of the 13th)

Austrian Cabinet Reorganized: Chancellor Schuschnigg Becomes Dictator; Vice-Chancellor Starhemberg Loses Power; Italian Influence in Austria also Shaken 11

Vienna: The Austrian cabinet has undergone a significant reorganization. Chancellor Dr. Kurt Schuschnigg has assumed control of both the Foreign and Defense Ministries, effectively becoming Austria's sole dictator. The cabinet deliberated for ten hours. According to a semi-official statement released at 0:45 this morning, the cabinet resolved that all critical domestic and foreign political matters should be handled by Dr. Schuschnigg. This move aims to forcefully concentrate all the forces preparing to build Austria and provide political cover to all those in Austria who support national independence. The main lines of Austria's domestic and foreign policies... However... It is said that the most noteworthy aspect of this cabinet reshuffle is the loss of power by Vice-Chancellor Starhemberg. (Reuter, 14th)

(Vienna) The Austrian cabinet was suddenly reorganized, with Chancellor Dr. Kurt Schuschnigg becoming Austria's sole dictator and ousting Interior Guard leader Vice-Chancellor Starhemberg from the government. This is in fact a victory of democracy over fascism. The cabinet deliberated for ten hours, adjourning late last night, before announcing the cabinet reshuffle. According to a semi-official statement, this move stems from policy differences between Schuschnigg and Starhemberg. Schuschnigg's policies are based on democratic principles, which clash with Starhemberg's. Starhemberg also opposed the disarmament of the Interior Guard. Starhemberg initially served as Vice-Chancellor in the Dollfuss cabinet. After Schuschnigg took office as Chancellor, Starhemberg continued in this role, attempting to expand his power in the hope of becoming Austria's dictator, but unexpectedly suffered a defeat. This cabinet reshuffle will significantly diminish the influence of fascism in Austria. (Reuter, 14th)

(Vienna) Chancellor Schuschnigg suddenly reorganized the cabinet at 3:30 this morning, removing Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg and Foreign Minister Weidengg from the new cabinet. Furthermore, members will be assigned to preside over the Patriotic Front led by Prince Starhemberg. The new cabinet is the third cabinet led by Schuschnigg. Its members are as follows:

Chancellor and Minister of Defense and Foreign Affairs: Kurt Schuschnigg

Vice-Chancellor and Minister of Interior: Baron Fielers (Patriotic Front member concurrently serving as Minister of Interior)

Minister of Justice: Hammerstein (newly appointed)

Minister of Education: Dengtona (reappointed)

Minister of Social Welfare: Breichu (former Minister without Portfolio)

Minister of Finance: Traxlsou (reappointed)

Minister of Commerce: Studqing (reappointed) (Havas, 14th)

(Vienna) Vice-Chancellor and Interior Guard leader Starhemberg is now replaced by Major Babarenfielers, who concurrently heads the Ministries of Interior and Public Security. As for Starhemberg's position as supreme leader of the "Fatherland Front," it is taken over by Dr. Schuschnigg. The "Fatherland Front" is the national party founded by the late Dr. Dollfuss. (Reuter, 14th)

(Vienna) Chancellor Schuschnigg suddenly reorganized the cabinet this morning. Only the position of Minister of Agriculture remains undecided. Recently, former cabinet member Fordmer was appointed to this position, completing the organization of the new cabinet. It does not include any members of the Greater German Party, which is no different from the previous cabinet. Fordmer belongs to the Catholic Social Party. (Havas, 14th)

(Vienna) Responsible sources have recently provided explanations regarding Chancellor Schuschnigg's cabinet reshuffle. It is said that former Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg sent a telegram to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini yesterday in the name of "the Austrian people fighting for Fascism," congratulating him on the successful annexation of Abyssinia. The wording strongly favored Fascism and severely criticized democracy, without seeking prior consent from cabinet members, which was deemed inappropriate. Foreign envoys stationed in Austria also expressed their dissatisfaction as a result. Chancellor Schuschnigg then resolutely reorganized the cabinet, ousting Prince Starhemberg from the new cabinet. Furthermore, well-informed sources say that Schuschnigg and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini have a close friendship and are unlikely to have misunderstandings as a result of this. (Havas, 14th)

(London) Diplomatic circles believe that the main reason for the reorganization of the Austrian cabinet is that Italy, under pressure from sanctions, has had to reduce its subsidies to the Austrian Home Guard (i.e., Austrian Fascists). The enthusiastic telegram sent by Starhemberg to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini on Sunday, congratulating him on the annexation of Abyssinia, was also a factor in promoting the cabinet reshuffle. Italy has always regarded Starhemberg as a pro-Italian leader, and is quite anxious to hear of his downfall, while France is gladly celebrating, believing that Austria's independence can be strengthened by this change. Germany welcomes Starhemberg's departure, but regrets that the Social Democratic Party has gained power in the new Austrian cabinet. (Reuter, 14th)

(Vienna) Chancellor Schuschnigg suddenly reorganized the cabinet and removed Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg from the new cabinet. The process is worth noting. Previously, Chancellor Schuschnigg led members of the Free Federation (i.e., Catholic labor groups) in a spring parade last Sunday. Hundreds of Interior Guard members (whose leader was Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg) hurled insults at him. The next day, the Chancellor still urged Prince Starhemberg to rectify discipline in a friendly manner. Until yesterday, although there was talk of reorganizing the cabinet, the Chancellor's intention was only to change a few minor cabinet members and reorganize the Patriotic Front. He still intended to maintain the dual leadership with Prince Starhemberg. Unexpectedly, Prince Starhemberg sent a telegram to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in the name of "the Austrian people fighting for Fascism," congratulating him on the successful annexation of Abyssinia. The wording severely criticized democracy, without seeking prior consent. The Chancellor found Starhemberg's excessive actions unbearable and declared last night that he would concurrently serve as Foreign Minister to eliminate negative impressions abroad and directly lead the Patriotic Front to stabilize domestic public opinion. This is the reason for the sudden reorganization of the cabinet this morning. From now on, Austria's dual leadership has been transformed into a dictatorship. In terms of its political program, all Austrians, regardless of their political views, should unite and work together for Austria's independence. (Havas, 14th)

(Vienna) Dr. Kurt Schuschnigg is only thirty-nine years old. He came to power after the Vienna tragedy in July 1934, when Dr. Dollfuss was murdered. He was awarded several medals for his outstanding military service in the European War. When he was a first lieutenant in the heavy artillery, he was captured by Italian soldiers. Shortly after, the European War ended. Dr. Schuschnigg was released back to Austria in 1919, practiced law, and was elected as a member of parliament in 1927, and then became a member of the Judiciary Committee. During the constitutional reform of 1929, Dr. Schuschnigg's speeches were well-received, and his name became well-known. He served as Minister of Justice in 1932, and concurrently as Minister of Education in 1933. The following year, he succeeded Dollfuss as Chancellor, and became a world figure. (Reuter, 14th)

British Cabinet in a Difficult Position; Part of the Public Attacks Baldwin 12

(London) Political figures stated tonight that the difficulties encountered by the cabinet are now extremely serious, but observing the political situation, it is not impossible to find a solution. There are roughly five major difficult issues. First, the Italian-Abyssinian problem requires a glorious solution that does not increase the disputes between Britain and Italy, and also maintains the prestige of the League of Nations. This matter is inherently complex and difficult to handle, but the cabinet should face the difficulties head-on. Former Foreign Secretary Sir Austen Chamberlain delivered a speech in the House of Commons last week, in which he strongly advocated for the abolition of sanctions, but the majority of public opinion still does not agree with this view. At this time, public sentiment is strongly supportive of Abyssinia, while political circles want to ease relations between Britain and Italy. The cabinet's task is to mediate between the two. Second, while the cabinet's task regarding the Italian-Abyssinian problem is extremely important, the actions taken by the German National Socialist Party are sufficient to endanger the status quo in Europe. Weighing the importance, the German problem is naturally a threat at the elbow, while the Italian-Abyssinian problem is relatively minor. As for the British proposals presented, there have been unfavorable reactions from the German side. The German reply is expected to be issued at the end of June. Third, the conflict between Palestinian Arabs and Jews is causing the cabinet to feel uneasy, but the actual situation is not as serious as people say. The cabinet decided on Sunday (the 11th) to send additional troops to be dispatched soon to strengthen the defenses. It is expected that order there will be restored soon. Fourth, the election results of the Egyptian House of Representatives, in which the Nationalist Party won a great victory, is regrettable from the British perspective, but the conclusion of the Anglo-Egyptian agreement should not be affected. Fifth, regarding the leak of the budget bill, if certain cabinet members are indeed guilty as a result of the investigation, then the Baldwin cabinet should resign. However, as of now, the investigation is not focusing on the responsibility of cabinet members, and it is too early to speculate on the outcome of the case. If Baldwin were to retire, then the position of Prime Minister would likely be promoted to the current Finance Minister Chamberlain. (Havas, 13th)

(London) It is well known that Prime Minister Baldwin is in a difficult position. The Daily Express recently launched an attack on him. It is futile to seek them in the cabinet, and there is no one in the front rows of the House of Commons. (London) Regarding the leakage of budget information, Colonial Secretary Thomas and his sons have been implicated. The government organized a special court yesterday to handle the matter. Thomas appeared in court this morning and testified for forty-five minutes. It is said that "Since I entered politics, I have participated in the preparation of the budget more than nine times, which can almost break the general record. I have never heard of any leakage of information." It is regrettable that the outside world knew about the tax increase case in advance, but it is not true that this is related to my wife buying a house. Then, in response to the court's questions, he recounted his political experience and said that after the case occurred, a friend informed him that his son was also involved. He immediately summoned his son and questioned him strictly. His son said he knew nothing. He also said that when the budget information was leaked, it was during the Easter holiday. At that time, he was taking his family to the beach in Ferring for vacation and then went to Brighton. He never disclosed the budget information to anyone. After his son was implicated, he immediately asked Prime Minister Baldwin to investigate his son's business situation. As far as he knows, Sir Bowater, a member of Parliament, is one of his son's customers. The former had expressed to his son his deep concern about the impending increase in income tax rates. His son then told him that he had dealings with Lloyd's Insurance Company and would ask the company on his behalf if there was any way to deal with it. External rumors probably arose from this. After Thomas finished his statement, he agreed to submit his bank passbook and investment list for review at the request of the magistrate. (Fourteenth Havas Electric)

Palestine, Renewed Conflicts Between Jews and Arabs, Strikes and Work Stoppages Continue, Authorities Announce State of Alert 30

Jerusalem, The situation in Palestine, with the increasing turmoil between Arabs and Jews, has suddenly intensified, causing the situation to become tense again. The British authorities have announced a state of alert. Street traffic is prohibited from 8:00 PM until 6:00 AM the next morning to prevent incidents. As a result of today's conflicts, two Jews were killed. Upon hearing the news, the police rushed to the scene to maintain order. Arabs in the Old City held demonstrations in two places, which were dispersed by the police. Farmlands, crops, markets and houses were set on fire in various locations. The Arab strike and work stoppage movement has not ended, and those who dare to resist are often beaten. (Thirteenth Havas Electric)

Jerusalem Two elderly Jews were killed yesterday afternoon in the Old City of Jerusalem. The authorities have dispatched police reinforcements to the Old City to suppress the violence and have implemented a curfew, prohibiting pedestrians from entering the city between 8 PM and 6 AM. The overall situation in Palestine remains unstable, and the strike declared by the Arabs is still in effect. In order to minimize the danger of the overall situation, the British authorities have dispatched reinforcements from Egypt to Palestine. The first conflict between Arabs and Jews occurred on April 29. At the funeral of the two Arabs who were killed, the Arabs claimed that the deaths were caused by Jewish revenge, while the police believed they were the result of infighting among the Arabs themselves. (Fourteenth Reuters Electric)

Results of Presidential Primaries of Two Major U.S. Parties 31

Columbus, Ohio, According to the latest results of yesterday's Republican presidential primary, Borah was only able to secure six delegates out of the fifty-two delegates to the national convention in this state. The remaining forty-six were supporters of Taft. On the Democratic side, in the 6,983 precinct primaries that have been announced, Roosevelt received a total of 401,753 votes, while his conservative opponent, Breckinridge, received a total of 27,512 votes. (Thirteenth National Electric)

(Washington) The Republican presidential campaign will also focus on unemployment relief, and this relief plan seems to be influenced by Senator Vandenberg's proposal. Vandenberg's plan is to abolish the current purely work-for-relief method and supplement it with pure relief, with the federal government allocating funds to the states, and the states raising 25% themselves to implement relief. A majority of Republican members of Congress believe that this method is more economical, so they hope it will become a reality. (Thirteenth National Electric)

Ancient Artifacts Transported to Shanghai Via Hong Kong; Zheng Tianxi and Others Accompany the Vessel for Care 43

At 5 p.m. that afternoon, the same ship transported them to Shanghai for exhibition in Beijing. Zheng Tianxi, Tang Xifen, and Zhuang Shangyan accompanied the ship for care. According to Zheng, this time 1,022 ancient artifacts were transported to the UK for exhibition, divided into 91 boxes. The exhibition lasted for 16 weeks, and more than 400,000 people visited, an unprecedented event. People from the United States and Germany even chartered special ships to visit. Foreigners praised our country's ancient artifacts and admired them endlessly. After deducting various expenses, half of the ticket revenue from the Arts Exhibition was allocated to our country to promote Sino-British cultural exchange. As for the seat of the international judge at The Hague, it will be decided after the election by the League of Nations. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 14th)

Hu Hanmin Dies in Guangzhou; Suffers Cerebral Hemorrhage, Faints, and Medical Treatment Fails; Dictates Will to Xiao Focheng During Crisis; Coffin Sealed at Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall on the 13th 65

Guangzhou Correspondence: After returning from Europe, Mr. Hu Hanmin immediately returned to Guangzhou and resided in Yan Garden in Dongshan. He repeatedly discussed national policies with the southwest party and government authorities to cope with foreign affairs and the current critical situation. However, after Mr. Hu contracted an illness in Hong Kong, although he went abroad for half a year of recuperation, the disease was not eradicated. After returning to Guangdong, the old illness recurred from time to time. In the past week, the weather here has changed, and the temperature has been inconsistent. Mr. Hu's sick body was again affected by the adverse weather, and the old illness suddenly broke out. Chinese and Western doctors were helpless, and he died at 7:40 p.m. on the 12th of this month. It is truly regrettable. Previously, Mr. Hu suffered from high blood pressure on the 9th of the month, but he was still able to go to his brother-in-law Chen Rong's home, Yong Garden, to chat and play chess when he was in the mood. However, due to excessive use of his brain, he fainted once at Chen's house that night. His family immediately summoned doctors Yang Zixiang and Chen Yiping for diagnosis and treatment. At that time, the examination showed a systolic blood pressure of 210 mmHg and a diastolic blood pressure of 135 mmHg, with left-sided hemiplegia. He was diagnosed with right-sided cerebral hemorrhage. Artificial ice was immediately applied to his head. At about 10 p.m., he regained consciousness. Mr. Hu seemed to know that he would not recover, so he immediately summoned party, government, and military leaders such as Xiao Focheng, Zou Lu, Chen Jitang, Lin Yunhai, Yang Xiji, Chen Yaoyuan, Chen Jiayou, Liu Jiwen, Huang Jilu, Zhang Renmin, Lin Yizhong, Chen Rong, Wang Jiwen, Hu Yisheng, and Mrs. Hu, Chen Shuzi, and his daughter, Hu Mulan, to his bedside. He dictated his will, which was recorded by Xiao Focheng. After dictating his will, Hu appeared very anxious, scratching his head frequently, and making gestures as if he wanted to get up. He also called his family to help him return home. The doctor used injections to treat him and help him sleep. On the morning of the 10th, his condition worsened, and he became unconscious. His family again invited doctors Bairnuohe and Huang Xizhang for diagnosis and treatment. They all agreed that his heart was weak and injected cardiac stimulants. In the afternoon, Deng Zhende, director of the Guangzhou Municipal Health Bureau, and Chinese medicine doctor Huang Shengshan arrived for diagnosis. All the doctors' judgments were the same. On the 10th, Hu's condition still did not improve. By the afternoon of the 11th, it became critical. His pulse was intermittent, his systolic blood pressure increased to 230 mmHg, his diastolic blood pressure was 150 mmHg, his temperature increased to 40.02 degrees Celsius, and his pulse increased to 135 beats per minute. His respiration was 42 breaths per minute. On that day, doctors Chuan Lin and Chi Zheng were invited to diagnose him again, and they all focused on strengthening his heart and preventing pulmonary congestion and other complications. By the 12th, pulmonary congestion symptoms did indeed appear, his body temperature increased to 40.7 degrees Celsius, his pulse reached 140 beats per minute, and his respiration reached 46 breaths per minute. In the afternoon, his breathing became more rapid, reaching 56 breaths per minute, his pulse reached 160 beats, and his systolic blood pressure suddenly dropped to 140 mmHg, while his diastolic blood pressure was 90 mmHg. Although injections were frequently administered, his heart gradually failed, and he died in Yong Garden (Chen Rong's residence) at 7:40 p.m. on the 12th. Mrs. Hu, Chen Shuzi, and her daughter, Mulan, cried in grief. Party, government, and military officials all went to Yong Garden to offer condolences. They then decided to send Mr. Hu's body to the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall for the coffin to be sealed. The body was transported by ambulance from the Municipal Hospital. Party and government officials Zou Lu, Chen Jitang, and Lin Yunhai all walked alongside to escort it. After entering the memorial hall, the body was placed in the main hall. Mr. Hu's body was dressed in a blue padded long robe and a black padded satin mandarin jacket. At about 9 p.m. that night, party, government, and military officials Zou Lu, Lin Yunhai, Chen Jiayou, Yang Xiji, Qu Fangpu, Lin Yizhong, Hu Yisheng, Zhang Renmin, Chen Yaoyuan, Huang Jilu, Yu Hanmou, Miao Peinan, Huang Linshu, Gan Jiehou, Liu Jiwen, Chen Rong, Li Xiangen, Cui Guangxiu, and others held a meeting in the east building of the memorial hall and organized the Hu Chairman Funeral Committee. The committee was divided into three sections: general affairs, finance, and secretarial, to handle the funeral affairs. It was also decided that Mr. Hu's body would be covered on the left and right with the party and national flags, and the coffin would be sealed at 4 p.m. on the 13th. All agencies inside and outside the province will cease all entertainment for one day from the 13th and fly flags at half-mast for three days to express mourning. (May 13th)

Japan's New Southern Policy of Southern Advancement: Establishment of Two Colonial Companies in Taiwan and Nanyang; Purpose of the Movement to Teach Chinese in Taiwan 66

Xiamen Correspondence: The Japanese naval authorities advocate defending the north and advancing to the south. Therefore, the Japanese cabinet discussed and agreed with the army and navy to place the focus of the southern advancement policy on Taiwan. This can be realized immediately after the special parliament currently in session passes it. The initial point of contention was whether to merge the Nanyang mandated territories under the jurisdiction of the Taiwan Governor-General and abolish the Nanyang Agency, or for the Nanyang Agency to remain independent while Taiwan would be responsible for the development of "Nanhua" and the "Outer Nanyang" north of the equator, and the Nanyang Agency would be responsible for the development of the "Inner Nanyang" south of the equator. The Japanese cabinet and the army strongly advocated unifying the southern advancement policy, so they advocated placing the entire Nanyang Agency under the control of the Taiwan Governor-General. The Ministry of Colonial Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy opposed this. The Ministry of Colonial Affairs believed that the mandated territories were not territory and that merging them would turn them into territory, which would violate the constitution. The Navy believed that the most important military and economic areas for southern advancement, Borneo, New Guinea, and the Dutch East Indies, were all in the "Inner Nanyang" south of the equator, and the Nanyang Agency was close to them, making it most suitable for overseeing their development. Taiwan was too far away, and it would be difficult to remotely manage them effectively. Recently, after several compromises by the cabinet, a new plan called the "New Southern Policy" was established. Its main points are: To change the traditional Taiwan governance policy, which places the political center in Taipei and the economic center in Keelung, and place the economic center in Kaohsiung instead (note that Keelung is in the northernmost part of the island of Taiwan, and Kaohsiung is in the southernmost part), making it the economic headquarters for the South Pacific. To make Kaohsiung the center of communication between the Nanyang mandated territories and Taiwan, establish a new regular shipping route between the two to ensure close contact. To this end, a "Taiwan Colonial Company," which will be the central guiding organization for this economic development policy, is submitting a bill to the current parliament for immediate realization. To establish a "Nanyang Colonial Company" (which can be regarded as a sister company to the Taiwan Colonial Company), submit a survey fee to the current parliament as a supplementary budget, and immediately establish it by order of the Nanyang Agency, with its headquarters in Palau (the capital of the mandated territory). At the same time, regarding the expansion of the Taiwan Governor-General's Office, it is planned to raise the Governor-General's status to the same as that of the Korean Governor-General. Although this new plan does not abolish the Nanyang Agency, the political and economic center is clearly still placed in Taiwan.

The Taiwan Colonial Company's organization will have a total capital of 30 million yuan, with the government contributing half, 15 million yuan. It is planned to allocate land and uncultivated wilderness and mountain forests of Taiwan official lease with a value of 15 million yuan to fill it. Hiratsuka, the chief of general affairs of the Taiwan Governor-General's Office, is currently in Tokyo attending the parliament and compromising with the cabinet regarding this case. The Taiwan Governor-General's Office held a meeting of the heads of the departments on May 3 and decided to organize a "Committee for the Evaluation of Government-Owned Property" to evaluate about 40,000 acres of government-leased land and uncultivated wilderness and mountain forests on the island of Taiwan. The company's business is defined as agriculture, forestry, immigration, and other businesses necessary for development. Coinciding with this is the movement to teach Chinese in Taiwan, which plans to abolish the English curriculum in schools and replace it with Chinese. The reason is that the targets of the southern advancement are Nanhua and Nanyang. Those who control the economic power in these two areas are mostly Fujianese and Cantonese people, and overseas Chinese from these two provinces. The Taiwanese are of the same ethnicity and culture as them and will inevitably stand in the forefront of southern development. Therefore, Chinese is necessary. The regular air route between Taipei and Bangkok, Thailand, was implemented this year. From this year (Showa 11) onwards, a subsidy of 144,400 yuan will be provided until the 20th year of Showa, for a total subsidy of 4,488,800 yuan over ten years. In short, Japan's aggressive southern advancement policy is not limited to Nanhua but covers the entire Nanyang, both north and south of the equator, and encompasses everything up to Singapore. This is evident in its strengthening of Taiwan and its mandated territories in the Caroline Islands, as well as its close ties with Thailand. (May 14th)

Recent Situation of Road Construction and Water Management in Fujian Province; Striving to Develop Important Highways; Water Conservancy Agencies Measuring Water Levels 67

Fuzhou Correspondence: Previously, the highway construction in this province was suspended from the second half of the 24th year (that is, from January of this year) due to financial difficulties. Recently, due to orders from the central government, highways are important and should still be constructed in sections to facilitate transportation. Therefore, the authorities in this province are resuming the gradual development of highways. The work plan is to first construct the main lines and then to repair and complete the original lines. According to news from the Provincial Highway Engineering Office, there are three main highways in this province: the Fuzhou-Quanzhou-Xiamen line, the Pucheng-Jian'ou-Yanping line, and the Fuzhou-Gutian-Jian'ou line. The Fuzhou-Quanzhou-Xiamen Road has been divided into the Fuzhou-Quanzhou and Quanzhou-Xiamen sections since it was taken back by the Construction Department for official management. Currently, the bridges and road surfaces of the entire line need to be actively repaired. The total cost is estimated to be more than 300,000 yuan, and a portion of the work has already started. The original allocated road maintenance fee for the Pucheng-Jian'ou-Yanping Road was 5,000 yuan per month, but this included the Chong'an-Jianning, Yanping-Jianning, and Shao'an-Jianning roads, which was a drop in the bucket. However, in order to facilitate traffic between Fujian and Zhejiang, the road surface and bridges of this line urgently need to be repaired. The estimated cost is more than 600,000 yuan, and the work has already begun gradually and should be completed separately in the autumn. As for the Fuzhou-Gutian-Jian'ou line, the total length is 234 kilometers, and the estimated construction cost is 850,000 yuan. It is currently being actively planned and is scheduled to start construction on July 1 and will take eight months to complete. After this line is completed, it will be extremely convenient for traffic between Fujian and Zhejiang. In addition, for other important highways, such as the highway from Liancheng to Jianning and other counties, the Construction Department has dispatched a surveying team to complete the surveying. The highway from Yong'an to Datian and other counties has already begun surveying. The office is currently planning the charts and plans. Once these several lines are completed, the provincial highway network will reach a considerable level of completeness.

In terms of water management, the upper reaches of the Minjiang River often experience seasonal rains in early summer, causing the river to swell and rush down, flooding the plains of Fuzhou, causing significant losses as fields and houses are submerged. During the flood season last year, the General Water Conservancy Engineering Office dispatched a flow measurement team to measure the flood flow and sediment content of the Minjiang River at Zhuqi and Guanyinting along the Minjiang River, in order to study the amount of water coming from the upper reaches as preliminary design data for guiding and managing the Minjiang River. The flood season has arrived again this year, and the measurement of flow and water level ranges of various streams has been further expanded. In addition to still setting up flow measurement stations in Zhuqi and Guanyinting, a flow measurement station has also been added to the Yongfu River. Water gauges have been installed along the river in Shuiji, Fengle, Jianyang, Nanping, Shaxiankou, Shaxian, Shunchang, Youxikou, Shuikou, Minqingkou, and other places to measure the rise and fall of floods. Daily and nightly records will be kept at Nanping, Shuikou, Zhuqi, Guanyinting, Wanbianjiao, Xiadou, Mawei, Nantai, and Hongshanqiao without interruption. In addition, an engineer will be stationed in Yanping to inspect the water level records in various places, investigate the drought and flood conditions in various counties, and the water conservancy projects that should be carried out, as well as the navigation issues of various streams. The surveying team departed for various places on the 12th of this month to begin work. The office has also formulated temporary regulations for flow measurement and ordered the team to comply with them. (May 13th)

Regulations for Flood Prevention along the Ejiang River: County Magistrates to Serve as Flood Prevention Commissioners, Establishment of Flood Control Sections and Allocation of Strong Laborers 68

Hankou Correspondence: Regarding flood prevention measures for the main embankments of the Yangtze and Xiang Rivers in Hubei Province, Qin Fen, Secretary-General of the National Economic Council, previously visited and agreed with the Provincial Government on six principles. The Provincial Government separately ordered their implementation. Currently, the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, recognizing the imminent arrival of the high-water season and the urgent need for flood prevention planning, has drafted "Flood Prevention Regulations for the Main Embankments of the Jianghan River" based on the aforementioned principles. These regulations have been submitted to the Provincial Government for approval at a meeting and will be promulgated to all counties with embankments for compliance. The content of the flood prevention regulations specifies that the flood prevention period will be from June 1st to the end of August as a standard, but may be adjusted according to the rise and fall of the water level. All flood prevention matters for the main embankments of the Jianghan River will be overseen by the county magistrates of the respective counties with embankments, serving concurrently as flood prevention commissioners. Furthermore, the district heads of each district with embankments will be appointed as flood prevention committee members, supervising the embankment repair and defense offices in their duties. As for flood prevention matters in cities and towns related to the main embankments of the Jianghan River, except for Wuhan City, which will be handled separately, the remaining cities and towns will be managed by their respective Chambers of Commerce or public works agencies, under the direction of the local government and the Jianghan Engineering Bureau's engineering offices. County magistrates serving concurrently as flood prevention commissioners should, before May 15th, jointly with the director of the relevant engineering office or their representative, re-examine and supplement the organization of the embankment repair and defense offices within their jurisdiction, as well as the selection of their directors and embankment watchmen. District heads and flood prevention committee members will be responsible for supervising and ordering responsible personnel to defend against floods, and will order the Baojia heads near the embankment line to assist in all matters. When special dangers occur in important embankment sections, the county magistrate and district head should personally go to the embankment section and jointly monitor the defense with the engineering office. Before the end of May, each embankment repair and defense office, acting under the instructions of the relevant district head or in consultation with the joint Bao chiefs, should allocate a certain number of fixed laborers per embankment protection unit, according to the dangerous embankment sections, from the strong laborers within the protection area. A register should be created and kept on file, and each laborer should be notified to equip themselves with items such as rain hats, raincoats, hoes, baskets, and shoulder poles. In case of minor dangers, groups will be called to the embankment for defense in shifts. In case of major dangers, all groups will go to the embankment simultaneously. In case of special dangers, each protection unit and group will assist each other in defense. Before the end of May, each embankment repair and defense office, acting under the instructions of the relevant district head or in consultation with the joint Bao chiefs, should investigate and register the names, items, quantities, prices, storage locations, and willingness to donate or sell items stored by residents within the protection area that can be used for flood prevention, such as lanterns, reed stalks, bamboo poles, rice straw, yellow beans, soybeans, ropes, hammers, wooden tampers, stone rollers, iron pots, and torn cotton, so that they can be requisitioned at any time after the flood prevention materials are exhausted. Each embankment repair and defense office should assign laborers to each embankment protection unit to patrol in shifts day and night. If a new danger is discovered, a warning is received, or instructions for emergency rescue are given, the unit responsible for defending the embankment should immediately sound the alarm, summon the laborers, supervise the work, and, if necessary, request the assistance of the Baojia head or the military police security team. The engineering offices of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau should, according to the dangerous and safe conditions of each embankment, establish a flood prevention section every 40 kilometers on average within the original sections. In addition to one section being concurrently managed by the original resident embankment section engineering personnel, each remaining flood prevention section will be headed by one temporary engineer, and two supervisors, and several embankment guards. They will handle inspection, verification, guidance, protection, rescue, and reporting of local and upstream water level changes. At the beginning of flood prevention, each section engineer should, under the guidance of the director of the respective engineering office, jointly with the director of each embankment repair and defense office, lead the embankment directors and embankment guards to conduct an inspection, and report to the Jianghan Bureau and the Provincial Government for record-keeping, mapping the width of the embankment, the quality of the soil, the distance from the river, the presence of old leaks or new seepage, rat holes and ant nests, and previous breaches, distinguishing between special danger and secondary danger. Each section engineer should survey and estimate the earthwork for fortifying dangerous sections, including immersion platforms, cutting embankment tops, and planting grass on inner slopes, preparing the work. While reporting for verification, a date should be specified for the embankment repair and defense offices to requisition laborers to handle. Each engineering office or section should, during peacetime and at the time of danger, gather the directors and embankment guards of each embankment repair and defense office to explain the flood prevention guidelines, or convene public lectures for the public. Each engineering office and section should, according to the situation, prepare and purchase important materials for emergency rescue for necessary times. No wages or food expenses will be given for requisitioning civilian labor during the flood prevention period. Compensation may not be given for requisitioning civilian goods during an emergency. (April 13th)

Zhejiang Province Planning to Alleviate the Coal Shortage: Expanding Coal Mines Insufficient to Supply Consumption; Coal Deposits Upstream of the Qiantang River are Being Planned for Exploitation 69

Hangzhou Correspondence: The consumption of coal in the Hangzhou urban area has reached 300 tons per day and approximately 9,000 tons per month due to the recent surge in factories, shops, and residential users. White coal accounts for 60% of this, and bituminous coal accounts for 40%. Demand is even greater in winter due to its wider range of uses. Since the September 18th Incident, all 50+ coal merchants in the city have unanimously switched to using domestic coal. The source of white coal relies solely on transportation from Shanxi and Henan provinces to Zhejiang, while bituminous coal is supplied by coal mines in Shandong, Tianjin, and Anhui provinces. Sales have increased even more than before because a portion of the counties in the interior have gradually learned to use coal. In November of last year, shipments of Shanxi coal suddenly stopped. Recently, the supply from coal-producing areas has been limited, and market prices have skyrocketed. Hangzhou has experienced a coal shortage due to the lack of supplies. As a result, coal merchants jointly requested relief from the municipal government and the Department of Construction, and requested the government to order the Changxing Coal Mine to supply 20 tons of coal to each coal merchant per month as an aid. The Department of Construction dispatched mining expert Zhang Jianyu to the Changxing Coal Mine to investigate the detailed situation of coal production, and he has already returned to the province to report.

Changxing Coal Mine

The Changxing Coal Mine is the only coal-producing area in Zhejiang, located approximately 50 li from the county seat. There is a light railway from the mining area to Wulibao, to facilitate transportation. From Wulibao, it is transported to other ports via waterways. The mine was opened in 1915 with an initial capital of only 40,000 yuan. In 1919, the capital was increased to expand the scope, bringing the total capital to 2 million yuan. Operations were suspended for four years due to the war in 1923. In 1927, the Central Construction Commission took over the mine and operated it under government management, making significant improvements and gradually increasing production. However, the expenses were too high, making it difficult to maintain. In 1932, it was returned to private management. The 5 million yuan in assets paid by the government during the government operation were repaid by the Mining Production Office at 20,000 yuan per month, to be paid off in 48 months. The current total value of the mine's assets has reached 5 million yuan. Financially, it is maintained by the Qinyi Syndicate, formed by the Shanghai Siming Bank. The Construction Committee has also sent personnel to supervise. The monthly income can have a surplus of 20,000 yuan.

Three Coal Pits

The mine currently has three coal pits that are being actively mined: Simaodun, Dameishan, and Guangxing. Each can produce 500 tons of coal per day, with the highest monthly output being 16,000 tons and the lowest being 13,000 tons. If special processing is required, an additional 100 tons can be produced per day. The current inventory at Wulibao is 3,000 tons. Due to debt relationships, the mine has contracts with factories in Wuxi, Jiaxing, Suzhou, etc., and coal production must be supplied to these factories. It is estimated that the three mines already exploited contain approximately 400,000 tons of coal, which can be used for two years. Currently, the mining area office is actively preparing to open new coal pits. However, shifting the supply to meet the needs of the initial market is likely not feasible in reality.

Miners' Lives

Miners can be divided into two main categories: inland workers, who are electrical and mechanical workers and receive better treatment, and laborers, who are on a contract system, divided into surface workers and underground workers. Wages range from 6 jiao, 8 jiao, to 1 yuan, and are arbitrarily distributed by foremen. Laborers are exploited and dare not resist. Underground work is the hardest, with working hours reaching tens of hours per day. If accidents such as gas explosions occur, lives are at risk of destruction at any time. In case of death, the office provides a burial fee of 30 yuan per person. Currently, the total number of miners is approximately 300,000.

Alleviating the Coal Shortage

In order to fundamentally solve the coal shortage problem in Zhejiang Province, and since Changxing coal cannot increase production to supply consumption in the province, it is essential to find alternative coal sources. It is reported that the authorities have already surveyed a coal deposit site upstream of the Qiantang River in eastern Zhejiang, not far from Hangzhou, and plan to exploit it. The area can also utilize waterway transportation, making transportation costs economical. The Coal Industry Association has also been ordered to investigate and report the exact amount of consumption in detail for overall planning and relief efforts. (May 14th)

Songjiang: Public Burial for Martyr Wu 70

Wu Guangtian, the son of Wu Qianmei, the former magistrate of Jiading County, was just over twenty years old. In 1927, while studying at Southeast University in Nanjing, when the Northern Expeditionary Army was settling Shanghai and preparing to attack Nanjing, Wu secretly agreed with comrades to plan an internal response. He was heard by spies, arrested, and killed by Chu Yupu of the Feng Army. After the National Revolutionary Army captured Nanjing, the National Government specially approved the construction of a monument for Wu in Zhongshan Park in the capital, providing annual compensation and allocating funds for funeral expenses. He was given a public burial in his hometown. On the 14th, Wu was publicly buried in the Caihua Jing Cemetery in this city. Nearly five to six hundred people from the party, military, government, business, and academic communities attended the funeral.

Wuxi: Shanghai Insurance Experts Send Personnel to Investigate the Tailong Insurance Claim 71

The Tailong Flour Company in Putihama, Nancangmen, outside the East Gate of this city, suddenly caught fire due to an electrical fault the day before yesterday. All machinery and factory buildings were burned, with total losses exceeding 400,000 yuan. It is understood that the company had cargo fire insurance worth 150,000 yuan with the British-owned Taiping Insurance Company in Shanghai. The insurance company sent Chang to Wuxi yesterday (14th) morning to investigate, estimating losses of more than 20,000 yuan. The fire insurance for the industrial side was jointly insured by Shanghai insurance professionals, including companies such as Lu Yishi Mo, Empress, Lianna, Siming, and Yizhong, totaling more than 300,000 yuan. Yesterday, Lu Yishi Mo and other foreign firms sent Chinese representative Yao Xiongguan and foreigners to Wuxi to investigate the truth and photograph each department for record-keeping. They returned to Shanghai that day.

Chamber of Commerce Restores Copper Coin Market Price 72

In order to regulate the market price of copper coins, the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting yesterday of more than 20 representatives from banks, money shops, and relevant parties. Chairman Qian Sunqing presided over the meeting. After discussion, it was decided that the money shops association should comply with the order to resume business on the 15th of this month and disclose the market list. As agreed upon by the county government last year, the exchange rate per legal tender coin should not exceed 300 copper coins or be lower than 290 copper coins. The Chamber of Commerce will send a letter to the county government to report to the province for record-keeping, and will also send letters to the banking and money industries for compliance.

County Party Department Mediates the Foundry Worker Strike 73

Due to organizing a labor union, workers from 17 foundry factories, including Xicheng, Huasheng, and Longchang in this city, were laid off by the factory owners, leading to a strike. Factory representatives Chen Zikuan, Zhu Zhongnan, Wu Peilin, Xie Zhongzhang, Zhou Zisheng, etc., feared that the foundry workers would not return to work, causing unexpected incidents and greatly affecting the machinery industry. Therefore, they jointly went to the County Chamber of Commerce to request mediation and to the County Government to petition. The Secretary received them and promised to convey the issues raised to County Magistrate Long for review. However, this case requires the joint convening of a meeting between labor and management by the Party Department before mediation can be conducted. The representatives were satisfied and left. The Foundry Workers' Union also sent a letter to the Shanghai Foundry Industry Union requesting assistance. Upon receiving the letter, the Shanghai Union sent a representative to Wuxi to discuss mediation methods with factory representatives Chen Zikuan, etc., and to demand three points on behalf of the labor side: 1. All 22 workers who have been laid off by the factories should return to their original jobs; 2. If workers have no work to do, they should alternate days with those who are working, and the factory should provide meals for the laid-off workers; 3. Working hours should be from 7:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 5:30 PM. However, the management did not accept these conditions, so after a long discussion, they adjourned without result. At the same time, Fang Yuan of the County Chamber of Commerce, considering that it is an extraordinary period and the countryside is in need of machinery for irrigation, and that the foundry workers have suddenly gone on strike, which will inevitably reduce the country's production capacity, also sent a letter to the County Government requesting prompt dispatch of force to stop the strike and order an immediate resumption of work to eliminate potential risks. In order to mediate, the County Party Department convened representatives from labor and management at 10:00 AM yesterday (14th) for a discussion meeting. More than 10 representatives from the management side, including Zhu Zhongnan and Wu Peilin, attended, but no representatives from the labor side were present. Members Xu Chizi and Xiao Ruoqian persuaded them to resume work today (15th) first. All principles proposed by both parties will be discussed again at a meeting between labor and management on the 21st of this month. Currently, the management representatives have agreed to resume operations, but whether the labor side will agree to resume work is still a question.

Kunshan: Family Tragedy in Zhoushu: Husband and Wife Found Dead 74

Qian Gui, a farmer from Zhaozhuangjiao, Wanxiang Village, Eighth District of this county, and his wife, Wu, suddenly had an argument on the night of the second day of this month, which escalated into a physical fight. When the mother saw the situation was bad, she rushed outside to call for help. By the time neighbors heard the commotion and went to mediate, Qian Gui's wife had already fallen in a pool of blood. A sickle was left on the ground, presumably used by her husband to kill her. Qian Gui, realizing that he had caused a disaster, drowned himself in the river out of fear of punishment. The neighbors were shocked and, considering the matter involved human lives, immediately reported it to the local patrol station the next day, which in turn reported it to the county government, who sent personnel to investigate.

Changshu: Soy Sauce Industry Requests Ban on Inferior Soy Sauce 75

The soy sauce industry here has traditionally specialized in making soy sauce, wine, and lees, with thriving business each year. Unexpectedly, a type of chemical soy sauce has recently flooded the market. In Changshu alone, monthly sales reach over 30,000 jin, taking away 30% of the market share of traditional soy sauce. Subsequently, the soy sauce industry requested that the chemical soy sauce be sent to the Zhenru Forensic Medicine Institute for testing. It was determined that it contained large amounts of toxins and was unsuitable for flavoring. Based on this, the soy sauce industry is now making a large-scale petition, urging the government to ban its sale to benefit the industry.

Group of Sandbar Residents Petition in Wuxi 76

The residents of Shazhou City caused a major dispute by obstructing river works. Subsequently, the county government arrested 12 accomplices and sent them to the Wuxi Security Command for strict military trial. However, the leaders of the case, Tan Jiujin and Ding Shishu, are still at large. Among those arrested, there were some who blindly followed. Therefore, the day before yesterday, more than 60 residents of Shazhou, including old men, women, and children (including three with white hair), carrying flags, went to the Commissioner's Office in Wuxi to petition, demanding the release of the innocent. As the Commissioner was in Beijing on official business, Section Chief Sheng received them. The residents immediately knelt down and begged, and were promised that the case would be handled impartially and that those who were innocent would be released after interrogation. The crowd then regrouped and returned to Changshu.

Yangzhou: Petition to the Province for Funds to Repair the Guadong Embankment 77

Jiangdu County Magistrate Ma Zhenbang, considering that the riverbank stretches for dozens of miles and has been repeatedly repaired due to years of erosion by the river tide, gradually shrinking and damaging farmland, and that the boundary dispute caused by building the embankment is nothing but competition for interests, and that the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Bureau has included Guadong in the flood control area during the flood season, proves that the relationship is special and cannot be handled by the local people alone. In addition, the county's financial resources cannot provide assistance. It is imperative to ask the province to do its best to help. In addition to personally going to the province to meet with Shen Baixian, Director of the Department of Construction, to explain everything, he has also prepared a detailed document outlining the reasons and handed it to Shu Guohua, Director of the Construction Bureau, to bring to the Department, requesting prompt approval to forward it to the National Economic Council for handling, in order to seek long-term benefits for the people of Guadong.

Changes in Director and Deputy Director of Relief Institution 78

Zhang Yunhe, Director of the Jiangdu Relief Institution, and Deputy Directors Zhu Gan臣 and Guo Lanshi, have submitted their resignations to the county government. It is now reported that the county government has appointed Hong Keting as Director and Zhang Jichuan as Deputy Director. Wang Jizhi has also been appointed by the county as the head of the institution's orphanage.

Nantong: Turmoil in Four Rural Districts Completely Resolved 79

Townspeople in Qinzhao and Henggang and other rural districts in Tong County experienced a misunderstanding which arose out of population surveys. This resulted in popular unrest. The head security forces captured 17 persons. After several days of representatives from the Party, government and community bodies heading to rural areas to counsel the populus, with the exception of the four primary offenders who have been turned over for military adjudication, the remainder have been bailed out by the township chiefs. The turmoil in the four districts is now entirely resolved.

Gaoyou: Septuagenarian Hangs Himself 80

The elderly farmer Wang Lianyun, nearly seventy years old, from Sanlidun, Beigang Township, Seventh District of this county, has only one child, now thirty-two years old. He has several acres of land, which have been damaged by disasters. This spring, he lacked rice seeds and ordered his grandson to ask for a loan from relatives in Baoying, but was unsuccessful. He felt that there was no joy in life and that life was extremely difficult, so he harbored the thought of ending his life. On the night of the eleventh, he hanged himself in his room. It is truly tragic.

Ningbo: Piracy Rampant in Xiangshan Port 81

Fisherman Zhu Chongkun of Dagang Port, Yin County, and four or five companions sailed to the outer sea to fish a few days ago. They caught over a thousand catties of fresh goods and transported them back to Daishan Chongbing for sale. However, when the boat reached the Simaen ocean area of Xiangshan Port, it was suddenly robbed clean by pirate ships. Another fisherman, Zhu Ayuan, also had 12 yuan in legal tender, clothes, and over a hundred catties of ramie stolen. According to statistics, no fewer than five or six fishing boats have been robbed one after another.

Education Broadcast Special

Chemistry Lecture Series Part 2: Applications of Chemistry 82

— Chen Kezhong, Full-Time Translator at the National Compilation and Translation Bureau

Chemistry has a very close relationship with human life. The four basic needs of life, "clothing, food, housing, and transportation," and the various tools a nation needs for survival are almost all dependent on chemistry. Primitive humans only used leaves to cover their bodies and keep warm, ate raw meat and blood to fill their stomachs, built nests in trees to live, and traveled without boats or vehicles. But human intelligence is like a huge ship, continuously advancing with time. Such primitive humans can no longer exist in the world. Modern humans not only use clothing to keep warm but also use it to represent the level of civilization, as the ancients said, "clothing to adorn the body." When it comes to "adorning the body," the most important thing is the color of the clothes, and the dyes that express the colors rely on chemical research. As for food, it's not just about filling the stomach. We also need to study which foods are most effective for the body's nutrition and how to eat them without hindering health. These questions can only be solved through chemical research. Speaking of housing, so-called "cave dwellings" are certainly wrong, and even old-fashioned bamboo huts and thatched cottages are outdated. The main materials for modern houses are bricks and cement, and the manufacture of these two things also requires chemical research. As for transportation, the asphalt paved on the roads, the steel and cement needed to build bridges, the railroad tracks, and the raw materials used to manufacture various ships, vehicles, airplanes, etc., mostly rely on chemical research. Even the fuel that drives these means of transportation needs to be solved by chemists. In addition to clothing, food, housing, and transportation, maintaining health is also extremely important for human life. The medicines for preventing and treating diseases can only be obtained through chemical research. As for a country, to defend against attacks from others and ensure national peace, all the necessary tools also rely on chemistry. From these facts, we can see that chemistry is the source of human intelligence and the key to modern culture.

Since the uses of chemistry are so broad, it is certainly impossible to cover everything in a short time. Now, I can only discuss a few important issues with you.

Regarding the Issue of Food: Food and drink are the main problem of life. If the problem of food cannot be solved, all other aspects of life cannot be discussed. From a chemical point of view, this problem can be divided into two aspects: one is the problem of food production, and the other is the problem of food nutrition.

The problem of food production: Most of the major foods of mankind are derived from plants. The growth of plants is mostly maintained by nitrogen. Air is composed of nitrogen, oxygen, and other small amounts of gases, and nitrogen accounts for more than three-quarters of the content, so there is no fear of a lack of nitrogen supply. Unfortunately, most plants cannot directly absorb nitrogen from the air; they must rely on nitrogen compounds such as nitrates to grow. We know that ammonia is produced after the decay of animals and plants, escapes into the air, is dissolved by rain and dew, and comes down to fertilize the soil. However, this amount of ammonia is too small, and plants cannot use it directly. Later, after the British Warington research, we learned that the change of ammonia in the soil depends on microorganisms. These microorganisms attach to the soil and, through contact with the air, can promote the change of ammonia. This effect is like yeast turning sugars into alcohol. There are usually two types of such microorganisms: the first type first turns ammonia compounds into nitrites; the second type can turn nitrites into nitrates after contact with air. After becoming nitrates, plants can use them directly. Therefore, plowing and turning the soil is a very effective method for farmers, because this can turn the microorganisms and nitrites in the soil to the surface to contact with the air, so that nitrites become nitrates. People in the past only knew the benefits of turning the soil, but did not know where the benefits were. Now we understand. In addition, there is another type of microorganism that is attached to the roots of plants. The roots of plants such as soybeans, alfalfa, and other legumes have root nodules, which contain this microorganism. Therefore, when the soil that continues to grow wheat becomes depleted, as long as you switch to planting legumes or alfalfa, then the soil will become fertile again. However, this method of remediation is very limited. Most of the sources of nitrogen fertilizers rely on Chilean nitrate, but the world's population is increasing every day, and the Chilean nitrate that is relied upon is decreasing every day. Supplying unlimited consumption with limited sources will naturally lead to a shortage. Therefore, in 1899, the famous British scientist Sir Wm. Crookes once said that if everyone does not quickly find a way to absorb nitrogen from the air, then there will be a danger of famine in the world in fifty years. At that time, after his reminder, many chemists worked hard on such research, and as a result, the German Haber air nitrogen fixation method was invented. Therefore, during the European War, although Germany was blockaded on all sides and unable to import Chilean nitrate, the nitrogen needed for German fertilizers and gunpowder was not a problem. Nowadays, there is no agriculturally developed country in the world that does not use artificial nitrogen fertilizer. Everyone will understand after looking at the following statistics table (1930).

China's annual food imports exceed 300 million yuan, competing with cotton for the first or second position in imports. Although inconvenient transportation and uneven distribution are also part of the reason for the food shortage, it should not be so different. If something happens to the country and the seaports are blockaded, then we will be in danger of starvation. In recent years, the number of artificial fertilizer imports has also been very considerable. In 1924, the value of imported ammonium sulfate was more than 2.6 million yuan. Subsequently, it increased year by year. By 1930, the value of imported ammonium sulfate was more than 27 million yuan, an increase of ten times in seven years, with an average annual increase of 50 percent. Last year, the Yongli Company opened an ammonium sulfate factory in Pukou, with ample capital and a large scale. In the future, such leakages can be remedied to some extent.

Public Memorial Ceremony

Public Memorial Eulogy

The eulogy for yesterday's public memorial was written by Mr. Yang Shukan. The original text reads: "On the fourteenth day of May in the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, Yang Shukan and other comrades of the Chinese Nationalist Party, respectfully offer this sacrifice of clear wine and plain dishes before the spirit of Mr. Hu Zhantang, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, and offer this eulogy: Oh, eminent sir, born in Lingbiao, devoted to the Party and the nation, becoming a founding elder. In your prime, you pursued revolution, followed the Premier, and in the southern pacification campaigns, you cast aside the pen and rose up. You rejoined the military staff, and your writing flowed swiftly, completing ten thousand words at once, striking fear into the enemy. You legislated for the capital, safeguarding the people, orderly and structured, like a net with its cords. When border unrest was reported, and incursions were alarming, your extraordinary plans could not be realized, and deep sorrow filled your heart. Your travels in Europe spanned nearly ninety thousand miles, broadly observing other nations, further spurring your own efforts. Upon your return for a brief respite, you were promoted to the central leadership. Suddenly, a mountain collapsed, shocking and bewildering us, leaving us with no way to redeem you. Ten thousand people looked up to you, the Party lost its guide, like a fleeting image without substance. The spirit of the nation must advance, never retreat. Reading these final words, we wipe away tears. We summon your soul and offer sacrifices from this coastal corner, vowing to carry out your legacy, forever steadfast and unchanging. May you accept this offering."
